### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): generalize the plugin-kind mechanism — name-keyed storage + root-wins override (kind enabler)

The foundational enabler for externalizing name-keyed, overridable kinds (RDD-surfaced when scoping
the agent/sidecar extraction: the shared `uf.PluginKinds` was a NAMELESS append-list — fine for
package-group, whose `uf.Group` had zero readers, but agent's iterate catalog and sidecar's
overridable embedded `tailscale` are name-keyed, root-wins consumers the append-list silently breaks).

- **Name threading:** the node name (the node key) is threaded into the STORAGE KEY in `runPlugin
  Kind`, NOT into the validated body — `assembleEntityBody` is untouched, so the body stays nameless
  and `#<Kind>Input` + the self-contained-schema property are unchanged. (No `Operation`/proto field
  added — that would be a wire cascade + dead data; the host has `gn.name` locally at the store site.)
- **Name-keyed storage:** `UnifiedFile.PluginKinds` `map[string][]json.RawMessage` →
  `map[string]map[string]json.RawMessage` (kind → name → body), mirroring the `uf.Agent`/`uf.Sidecar`
  shape the consumers need.
- **Root-wins override merge:** `mergePluginKindsMap` rewritten from append → name-keyed override,
  byte-identical to `mergeSidecarMap`/`mergeAgentMap` (per kind, an existing root/project entry for a
  name is preserved; the embedded/import source fills only absent names) — this is what lets a
  project's `tailscale` sidecar override the embedded one once sidecar externalizes (Cutover B).

package-group's plugin needed no change (it decodes the nameless body); its tests + the external
`e3kind` test updated to the name-keyed form. The override is dormant until a name-keyed kind extracts
(Cutover B: agent/module/sidecar).

**MAIN-ONLY**: the name is the node KEY (not authored) — no schema/`#<Kind>Input` change, no `#Node`
change, no MigrationStep, no version bump, no cascade (zero codegen drift; `charly box validate` exit
0 at the unchanged schema version).

R10: `go test ./...` (incl. the new `TestMergePluginKindsMap_NameKeyedOverride` + `TestLoadUnified_
PluginKindNameOverride` — two docs, same name → root wins — plus the updated package-group/e3kind
tests) + `task build:charly` + `charly box validate` exit 0 + check-pod (loader/merge no-regression —
`mergePluginKindsMap` runs on every load).

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): externalize the 15-command deploy-lifecycle group into CommandProviders

The deploy-lifecycle command bulk: `start, stop, status, restart, update, remove, logs, shell, cmd,
cp, volume, service, config, bundle, reap-orphans` leave the hardcoded `var cli struct{…}` in
`main.go` and become dedicated `<name>Command` CommandProviders (`plugin_command_<name>.go`), each
`KongCommand()` returning the existing `<Name>Cmd` Kong struct verbatim. **The key insight: the Run
handlers — and the core deploy/bundle machinery they call (LoadBundleConfig, the deploy targets) —
are untouched; only the CLI registration location moves off the struct, so "coupling in the Run
handler" is not a blocker.** They self-register via `registerDedicatedBuiltin` and arrive through
`cli.Plugins`; the MCP surface auto-picks them up.

**Coupling audit (per-command `cli.<Field>` grep):** the ONLY command field read outside Kong
dispatch is `cli.Check.Plugins` (nested-command plugins) — so `check`, `feature`, `vm` are deferred
(large harness/domain commands; `check` has the real `cli.Check.Plugins` coupling). All 15
deploy-lifecycle commands are clean leaf moves. `reap-orphans` uses the safe filename
`plugin_command_reap_orphans.go` (underscore) with `Reserved()` returning the hyphenated CLI word.
Machinery (box/candy/clean/doctor/migrate/settings/version/__plugin) stays hardcoded.

**MAIN-ONLY**: zero codegen drift, no schema change, no version bump. GOOS-trap check: all 22
`plugin_command_*.go` compile into the linux build.

R10: `go test ./...` (incl. `TestCommandProviders_DeployLifecycleCommands` — 15 sub-cases asserting
exact `ctx.Command()` matches + collection + MCP-surface preservation) + `task build:charly` + sample
`charly {start,bundle,reap-orphans,cp} --help` live + `charly box validate` exit 0 + check-pod
(CLI-init no-regression). `charly --help` lists all 33 top-level commands, surface preserved.

moving `udev` off the struct would have silently DROPPED its 4 leaves (incl. the destructive
`udev.install`/`udev.remove`) from the MCP tools. Fixed by wiring `collectCommandPlugins()` into both
`mcp_server.go` `kong.New` sites (model build + tool-run parser) + the `buildTestKong` helper — so a
plugin command's tools survive in the MCP surface identically to a hardcoded one.

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): extract 3 schema-less IR providers (deploy-target/builder/step) into dedicated plugin files (Phase 3 pattern proof)

Proves the IR-provider → dedicated-plugin pattern with the cleanest candidate of each of the three
schema-less provider categories: `localTarget` (deploy:local), `cargoBuilder` (builder:cargo),
`rebootStepProvider` (step:Reboot). Each moves out of the shared `builtinProviderInstances` slice +
the `charly.yml` providers manifest into its OWN dedicated file (`plugin_deploy_local.go` /
`plugin_builder_cargo.go` / `plugin_step_reboot.go`) — the externalizable property — while dispatch
stays IDENTICAL through `providerRegistry.Resolve{Deploy,Step,Builder}` (pure registration-location
refactor, zero behavior change).

**RDD finding (the mechanism):** unlike verb/kind plugin units, IR providers carry NO authored input
→ NO schema, so a schema-less `RegisterBuiltinPluginUnit` is correctly REJECTED (`registerPluginUnit
Schema` hard-rejects an empty `CueSource` — that path is exclusively for schema-carrying authored
plugins). The dedicated mechanism: each provider self-registers via a package-var initializer
(`var _ = registerDedicatedBuiltin(localTarget{})`) which runs BEFORE any `init()`, so the bootstrap
bijection gates observe it without the file-name ordering race the shared-slice init deliberately
avoids — strictly more robust than an `init()`. This is the template for the Phase-3 bulk (the other
4 deploy targets, 11 steps, 3 builders).

**MAIN-ONLY** (no schema/corpus/cascade): no `schema/*.cue` edit, no `#Node`/`#Op` change, zero
codegen drift, no version bump. The per-class bijection gates (`checkDeployProviderBijection`,
`checkStepProviderBijection`) + `TestProviderManifest_EnforcedBijection` stay green (3 removed from
both manifest and slice).

R10: `go test ./...` (incl. the new `TestDedicatedProviders_ResolveAndDispatch` asserting each
resolves + dispatches + is absent from the shared slice/manifest, + the bijection gates that panic
the suite on a registration-ordering regression) + `task build:charly` + `charly box validate` exit 0
+ check-pod (registry-init + build-pipeline no-regression on the fresh binary).

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): extract the `package-group` KIND into a plugin unit (first Phase-2 kind extraction) + fix the kind→plugin loader scaffolding

The FIRST kind extraction, proving the kind→plugin pattern end-to-end through the real loader. The
zero-corpus `package-group` kind leaves the closed core into a dedicated builtin plugin unit
(`charly/plugin/builtins/package-group/` + `plugin_package_group.go`): its `#Group` schema moves
into the plugin's self-contained `#PackageGroupInput` .cue, and dispatch changes from the typed
`KindProvider.DecodeNode` to the generic plugin path (`normalizeNodeInto` → `runPluginKind` →
`Invoke(OpLoad)`, validated against the served schema, stored in `uf.PluginKinds["package-group"]`).
The authored form is UNCHANGED (`kind:` stays `kind:`) — kind extraction, unlike verb extraction,
needs no MigrationStep authoring rewrite.

**Zero-corpus → in-place, MAIN-ONLY, no version bump, no 6-repo cascade** (the EDGE-INHERIT cutover-C
precedent): no file authors `package-group:`, so the new schema accepts the whole corpus at the
unchanged `version: 2026.173.1742` — `charly box validate` exit 0 confirms it.

**Two loader-scaffolding bugs found via RDD + fixed in-scope (R1/R2):** (1) `mergeUnified` never
merged `PluginKinds`, so EVERY plugin-kind entity (incl. the existing external `e3kind` path) was
silently dropped on every load — added `mergePluginKindsMap` (append-merge). (2) `loadBuiltinPlugin
Units()` ran only on the check/deploy paths, not `LoadUnified`, so `runPluginKind`'s load-time schema
validation would fail "schema not loaded" — added an idempotent gate in `runPluginKind`. Both were
masked because the E3 kind-plugin scaffolding had only ever been tested by calling `normalizeNodeInto`
directly, bypassing the real loader.

**R5:** `uf.Group` had NO downstream reader (decoded + merged, never consumed — no Calamares generator
exists yet); removed `uf.Group`, `mergeGroupMap`, and the dead `GroupSpec` aliases. `spec.Group` stays
as the canonical entity type the plugin decodes into.

R10: `go test ./...` (incl. the new `plugin_package_group_test.go` driving a `package-group:` doc
through `LoadUnified` into `uf.PluginKinds` + the load-time schema-gate rejection test) + `task
build:charly` + `charly box validate` exit 0 + check-pod (loader no-regression on the fresh binary).

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly)!: extract the observe-only goss verbs (process/port/dns) into plugin units + schema HEAD → 2026.173.1742

The first BATCH of execution-needing goss verbs extracted into dedicated builtin plugin units
(via the runPluginVerb executor enabler — each keeps its live `*Runner`): **process, port,
dns**. Each leaves the closed `#Op`/`spec.OpVerbs`, becomes `plugin: <verb>` + `plugin_input`,
and reuses its existing `runX` impl (RunVerb decodes plugin_input → the typed `params.<Verb>
Input` → `runProcess`/`runPort`/`runDNS`). Shared fields stay in `#Op`, referenced standalone
in the plugin schemas (`reachable` port↔addr, `addrs` dns↔interface). Added the R3 shared
`decodePluginInput` helper.

One generalized MigrationStep `goss-verbs-to-plugin` (@ `2026.173.1741`, replacing the
single-verb `process-to-plugin`) drives a `gossVerbFields` set: a `check:` step carrying
`process:`/`port:`/`dns:` → `plugin: <verb>` + `plugin_input` (isStepNode-gated, so a box's
published `port:` and a candy's install `package:`/`service:` lists are NEVER touched;
idempotent). `calver-schema` + `LatestSchemaVersion` `2026.173.1616` → `2026.173.1742`;
re-stamped + cascaded across all 6 repos (B7).

**Architectural finding (R1, RDD-surfaced):** the state-provision goss verbs
(file/package/service/user/unix_group/kernel_param/mount) are NOT extractable into the
check-only `CheckVerbProvider` plugin model — they additionally carry a `RenderProvisionScript`
act form AND lower to install-plan steps (the package-install/service-enable timeline baked
into Containerfiles + every deploy). The plugin model has no act/install-lowering half, so
extracting them would silently drop `run: package:`/`run: service:` provisioning (a masked
regression). They stay base `#Op` verbs pending a plugin-model decision. The remaining
observe-only goss verbs (command/http/interface/addr) are batch-2.

R10: `go test ./...` (incl. `TestMigrateGossVerbsToPlugin` + converted `TestRunner_{Port,DNS,
Process}Plugin` + the bijection/schema-splice gates) + `task build:charly` + `charly box
validate` exit 0 across all 6 repos (every root at `2026.173.1742`) + check-pod (`plugin: port`
via the migrated check-stack-layer + the new `plugin: dns` step, live). 5 submodule pointers
bumped.

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): runPluginVerb dispatches CheckVerbProvider plugin units via RunVerb (executor enabler)

The `plugin: <verb>` dispatch (`runPluginVerb`) now type-checks the resolved provider: a
`CheckVerbProvider` plugin unit is dispatched via `RunVerb` (keeping the live `*Runner`), and
only an OUT-OF-PROCESS provider falls through to the serialized `Invoke` envelope. This
unblocks extracting the execution-needing goss verbs (`file`/`port`/`command`/…) — which call
`r.Exec` and need the `*Runner` — into builtin plugin units (the next Phase-1 step), the way
`matching` (pure, Invoke-based) already extracted.

Adds the canonical `examplerunverb` builtin plugin unit (a `CheckVerbProvider`, mirroring
`exampleprobe`'s Invoke form — the in-proc-RunVerb analogue) + `TestRunPluginVerb_CheckVerb
ProviderKeepsRunner`, which proves `RunVerb` ran (not the `Invoke` stub) by reading `r.Mode`
off the live `*Runner` — a value unreachable across the Invoke wire. Additive / dormant until
a goss verb extracts.

R10: `go test ./...` (incl. the new test + the builtin-schema-splice + reserved-word gates) +
`task build:charly` + `charly box validate` exit 0 (root + box/fedora) + check-pod (the new
`check-runverb-plugin` step exercises the path live on the fresh rebuild). box/fedora pointer
bumped.

### 2026-06-22 — style(charly): gofmt-align provider_kind_invoke_test.go (R2 hygiene)

A pre-existing gofmt brace-misalignment in the `e3KindTestProv` single-line method block
(`Reserved()`/`Class()`/`Invoke()`), surfaced while reviewing the matchers→SDK cutover, is
corrected with `gofmt -w` — whitespace-only, zero behavior change. The pre-commit gate does
not run gofmt, which is how it slipped in; the tree is now `gofmt -l`-clean. Verified:
`gofmt -l charly/` empty, `go test` (the e3kind kind-invoke test compiles + passes), `go
build`. No bed: a test-file format change has zero shipped-binary surface, so a `charly check
run` gate could not fail on it (waste, per R10's gate-by-change-class).

### 2026-06-22 — refactor(charly): goss matchers → the plugin SDK (the Phase-1 verb-extraction prerequisite)

The 5 pure goss-matcher functions (`matchAll`/`matchOne`/`matchNumeric`/`matchValueString`/
`matchValueStrings`, formerly in `package main` charly/checkrun.go) move into the plugin SDK
(`charly/plugin/sdk/matchers.go`) as `MatchAll`/`MatchValueString`/`MatchValueStrings`
(exported) + `matchOne`/`matchNumeric` (SDK-internal), with `type Matcher = spec.Matcher`
re-exported so an out-of-process verb plugin reaches the matcher contract through the SDK
ALONE. This is the prerequisite for extracting ANY check verb: external verb plugins cannot
import `package main`, so the single shared matcher implementation (core goss verbs AND
future external verb plugins — R3) has to live in the SDK first.

The 12 core call sites (checkrun.go ×6, checkrun_verbs.go ×4, checkrun_charly_verbs.go ×2)
now call `sdk.MatchAll`/`sdk.MatchValueString`. Two tests that called the now-SDK-internal
`matchOne` directly relocate from checkrun_test.go into the SDK package's matchers_test.go
(R5 — tests live with the code). The SDK now pulls `charly/spec` (→ `gopkg.in/yaml.v3`) into
its dependency closure, so the two out-of-tree example plugin modules
(`candy/plugin-example-{deploy,external}/go.mod`) gain `gopkg.in/yaml.v3 // indirect` — an
intrinsic consequence of routing `Matcher` through the SDK.

R10: `go test ./...` (full suite incl. the new `plugin/sdk` matcher tests + the two external
plugin e2e tests that build against the new SDK closure) + `task build:charly` + check-pod
(the disposable bed's `file`/`command`/`port`/`service` goss checks exercise `sdk.MatchAll`
live on the fresh rebuild — the moved matchers' actual consumer). The matcher operator set is
byte-for-byte unchanged; this is a pure relocation.

The `charly doctor` host-device description table (device path → human description, 8
entries) moves from the hardcoded Go var `deviceDescriptions` (doctor.go) into a
`device_descriptions:` directive in the embedded `charly.yml` — the Phase-4 "device tables"
data item. doctor.go reads it via `parseEmbeddedDeviceDescriptions()` over the shared
`unmarshalEmbeddedDefaults` helper; `#NodeDoc` (schema/node.cue) recognizes the directive;
`task cue:gen` regenerated spec. The `"/dev/dri/renderD*"` key is YAML-quoted (the `*`).

R10 (doctor-data-only — does not touch the deploy/build flow, so the matching live gate is
`charly doctor`, not a deploy bed): `charly doctor` renders the data-driven descriptions
live (`/dev/kvm -- KVM virtualization`, `/dev/dri/renderD128 -- GPU render node`, …);
`TestDeviceDescriptionsFromEmbedded` proves the loaded map matches the 8 canonical entries
(incl. the quoted `*` key); `go test ./...` + `task build:charly` + `charly version`
(init-parse, no panic) + `charly box validate` (repo, exit 0).

Extends the external-command-plugin path to NESTED commands, so the Phase-1 dep-shed targets
`charly check kube`/`adb`/`appium` can be served out-of-process (where their client-go /
selenium will live). RDD-proven first: `kong.Plugins` embedded in a NESTED command node
injects a dynamic `reflect.StructOf` subcommand there, not only at the CLI root.

`collectExternalCommandPlugins` now returns `(topLevel, nestedByParent, table)`: a
ClassCommand provider implementing the new `NestedCommandProvider` interface
(`CommandParent() string`) nests under that parent; everything else stays top-level. The
dispatch table is keyed by the full command PATH (`commandPathKey` strips Kong's trailing
` <args>`: `"check kube <args>"` → `"check kube"`), and main.go dispatches via that path key.
`CheckCmd` (check_cmd.go) embeds `kong.Plugins`; main sets `cli.Check.Plugins =
nestedByParent["check"]`. The dead `firstCommandWord` is removed (R5 — replaced by
`commandPathKey`).

R10: `TestExternalCommandSeam_NestedCheckCommand` builds a `NestedCommandProvider`, nests it
under a CheckCmd-shaped parent (kong.Plugins embed + a static sibling), parses
`check examplekube nodes --wide`, asserts the path key `"check examplekube"`, and confirms
the pass-through args reach Invoke; the top-level seam test + `TestCommandSeam_PluginCommand
Injected` still pass; `go test ./...` + `task build:charly` + `charly version` + `charly check
--help` (all 36 builtin check subcommands intact — empty nested embed is a no-op) + `charly
box validate` + check-pod (the live check-command + CLI-dispatch flow, no regression). Dormant
until a real nested command plugin registers (the kube/adb/appium extractions).

The enabler that unblocks the Phase-1 dep-shedding command extractions (`charly check kube`
→ client-go, `check adb`/`appium` → selenium, etc.): a command can now be served by an
OUT-OF-PROCESS plugin, not just a compiled-in `CommandProvider`. RDD-proven first
(`reflect.StructOf` builds a Kong-parseable command, the selected command is detectable, and
the parsed flags read back via reflection — GO).

`collectExternalCommandPlugins` (provider_command_external.go) builds a dynamic Kong
subcommand for every ClassCommand provider that is NOT a builtin `CommandProvider`: a
`reflect.StructOf` holder with one `cmd:""` field per command whose value is a pass-through
`Args []string` (the plugin owns its own flag parsing via its `.cue`). Because
`reflect.StructOf` types have no methods, these commands carry no `Run()` for Kong's
`ctx.Run()` — so main.go dispatches them MANUALLY after `kong.Parse`: when the selected
command's first word matches the dispatch table, `dispatchExternalCommand` forwards the
pass-through args to the provider's `Invoke` (the standard envelope); everything else runs
through `ctx.Run()` unchanged. The seam is dormant-but-tested until a real external command
plugin registers (the Phase-1+ extractions) — mirroring E3-kind / the builtin command seam.

R10: `TestExternalCommandSeam_DynamicCommandDispatch` builds a dynamic command, parses
`examplecmd nodes --wide`, and confirms the pass-through args (flag included) reach a fake
provider's Invoke; `go test ./...` (full suite, the builtin command seam unregressed) +
`task build:charly` + `charly version` (the CLI runs with the new machinery: empty external
table → normal dispatch) + `charly box validate` + check-pod (the live CLI-dispatch flow
exercises the new collect+table-check path with no external commands registered → `ctx.Run()`,
no regression).

The per-distro-family OVMF firmware candidate path pairs (fedora/arch/debian ×
secure/nonsecure × ordered {code, vars} candidates) move from inline literals in
`ovmfCandidatesForDistro` (ovmf_paths.go) into an `ovmf_paths:` directive in the embedded
`charly.yml`. Only the PATH DATA moves — the alias→family resolution (centos→fedora,
manjaro→arch, ubuntu→debian), the secure-boot selection, and the unknown-distro union STAY
Go logic in `ovmfCandidatesForDistro`, which reads the family table (`ovmfPathTable`) via
`parseEmbeddedOvmfPaths()` over the shared `unmarshalEmbeddedDefaults` helper. `#NodeDoc`
(schema/node.cue) recognizes the directive; `task cue:gen` regenerated spec.

R10 (the resolution is exercised LIVE on real host firmware — the correct gate, unlike a
BIOS VM bed which never touches OVMF): `TestResolveOvmfPaths_HostFirmwareResolves` runs the
exact path `charly vm create` uses — `ResolveOvmfPaths(hostDistro, secure)` →
`ovmfCandidatesForDistro` (now data-driven) → `os.Stat` — against the Arch host's real
firmware and confirms it resolves to existing `/usr/share/edk2/x64/OVMF_CODE.4m.fd` +
`OVMF_VARS.4m.fd`. `TestOvmfPathsFromEmbedded` proves `ovmfCandidatesForDistro` returns
byte-identical candidates (fedora-secure / arch-nonsecure / debian-secure / centos→fedora
alias / gentoo→union(6)). Plus `go test ./...` + `task build:charly` + `charly box
validate` (repo + box/fedora). The full UEFI VM-create boot is unchanged by construction
(byte-identical resolved paths); the live resolution against real firmware is the changed
behavior and it is verified.

Fixes a real teardown bug: `charly vm destroy`/`stop` reported success but left the
libvirt domain RUNNING, leaking the VM (surfaced when a failed disposable VM bed orphaned
its domain). Root cause in `gracefulStopDomain` (vm_libvirt.go): it early-returned on
`state != domainStateRunning` (so a paused/blocked/crashed domain got NO action), and its
running-path poll predicate was `serr != nil || state != domainStateRunning` — which
returns "done" on a *transient* shutdown-in-progress/paused state OR a transient
`domainState` RPC error, WITHOUT forcing. `VmDestroyCmd` then called `undefineDomain` on
the still-active domain, turning it into a lingering transient running domain.

The fix: poll for `libvirt.DomainShutoff` specifically (not merely "not running"), skip the
graceful ACPI path for non-running active states, and — the key guarantee —
force-`destroyDomain` unless the domain actually reached SHUTOFF before the caller
undefines it. The graceful-flush-first behavior for a healthy running guest (so the
in-guest podman overlay store flushes cleanly) is preserved; the force only fires when the
graceful path did not reach SHUTOFF.

Diagnosed empirically (a direct `DomainDestroy` drove the live stray domain 1→5
running→SHUTOFF, proving the hard kill works — the bug was never reaching it). R10:
`TestGracefulStopDomain_ForcesActiveDomainToShutoff` creates a real transient libvirt
domain, suspends it to PAUSED (the non-running active state the old code no-op'd on), runs
`gracefulStopDomain`, and asserts SHUTOFF (fails without the fix); `go test ./...` +
`task build:charly` + the fixed binary cleaned the actual orphaned stray VM
(running→SHUTOFF→undefined→gone, verified via `virsh list --all`). Follow-up recorded
separately: `charly vm destroy --disk` on a *running* VM deletes the disk before stopping
(should stop-first); and the failed-bed partial teardown that orphaned the domain.

The second Phase-4 data-out-of-Go cutover, via the pattern the first established: the
`charly doctor` host-dependency install-hint table (binary name → distro ID → package
name, 19 binaries) moves from the hardcoded Go var `installHints` (distro.go) into an
`install_hints:` directive in the embedded `charly.yml`. distro.go reads it via
`parseEmbeddedInstallHints()` over the shared `unmarshalEmbeddedDefaults` helper;
`#NodeDoc` (schema/node.cue) recognizes the directive (`{[string]: {[string]: string}}`,
added to the top-level-key regex); `task cue:gen` regenerated spec. The two colon-bearing
`"AUR: yay -S …"` values are YAML-quoted. `InstallHint`'s lookup/family-fallback/AUR logic
is untouched — only the map's source changed, so its output is identical.
`TestInstallHintsFromEmbedded` proves the loaded map matches canonically (count + the
quoted AUR values + spot-checks). R10: `go test ./...` + `task build:charly` (R9) +
`charly version` (init-parse runs, no panic) + `charly doctor` (exercises InstallHint LIVE
with the data-driven map) + `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora, exit 0) + check-pod
(no regression in the deploy flow).

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): context_ignore_baseline → the embedded charly.yml (Phase-4 data extraction)

The first Phase-4 data-out-of-Go cutover: the built-in build-context ignore baseline (the
16 VCS/binary-exclude + cache-hygiene globs that seed every image's `.containerignore` /
`.dockerignore`) moves from the hardcoded Go var `baselineContextIgnore` (generate.go) into
a `context_ignore_baseline:` directive in the embedded `charly.yml` — data, not code.
generate.go now reads it via `parseEmbeddedContextIgnoreBaseline()` over the new shared
`unmarshalEmbeddedDefaults` helper (R3: factored from the registry-manifest reader
`parseEmbeddedProviderManifest`, which now also uses it). `#NodeDoc` (schema/node.cue)
recognizes the directive (added to the top-level-key regex, mirroring `providers:`), so a
project may override the baseline too; `task cue:gen` regenerated spec. The
baseline-then-project-overlay merge semantics are unchanged — generate.go still overlays
`defaults.context_ignore` on top. `TestContextIgnoreBaselineFromEmbedded` proves the loaded
list matches the 16 canonical patterns byte-for-byte (the guard against drift / parse
breakage). R10: `go test ./...` + `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora, exit 0) +

live). R8: the emitted `.containerignore` is byte-identical to before (same patterns).

### 2026-06-22 — fix(charly): plugin-verb tests are self-contained — TestMain preloads the builtin plugin schemas

Test-only change (no production behavior). A new `TestMain` in the charly package runs
the sync.Once `loadBuiltinPluginUnits()` — the builtin plugin-schema load the binary does
at boot — BEFORE any test, so plugin-verb validation (`validateAuthoredPluginInput`) sees
the builtin `#<Word>Input` defs in EVERY test, not only when a sibling test
(`plugin_external_test.go`) happens to trigger the global sync.Once-filled `pluginSchemas`
first. Before this, `TestRunPluginVerb_Dispatch` and friends passed in the full
`go test ./...` suite but FAILED in a narrow `-run` subset (`no input def registered
(schema not loaded)`) — surfaced while landing the external-charly-verb dispatch enabler
(v2026.173.1058) and recorded there as a non-blocking follow-up. The loader is idempotent
(`builtinGateOnce`), so the existing sibling call is now a no-op. Gate: `go test` — the
previously-failing subset passes AND the full suite stays green; no bed (no production
code path touched).

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): external-charly-verb dispatch — a live verb word can be served by an out-of-process provider (no #Op migration)

The Phase-1 enabler that makes verb externalization ADDITIVE, not a schema migration.
A live verb word (cdp/kube/vnc/…) is authored in `#Op` (`kube: apply`, `namespace: demo`)
and dispatched in `checkrun.go` via `providerRegistry.ResolveVerb`. Previously a resolved
provider that was NOT a `CheckVerbProvider` (i.e. out-of-process) was SKIPPED with "no
in-process check handler". Now it routes to the Invoke envelope: the new shared
`invokeVerbProvider` (`provider_checkenv.go`) marshals the FULL Op + the check env and
calls `prov.Invoke(OpRun)`, decoding the `pluginCheckResult` — the SAME path the generic
`plugin:` verb uses (factored out of `runPluginVerb`, R3: two callers now).

The key consequence (corrects an earlier wrong assumption that verb extraction needs an
authoring migration): because the plugin is handed the full Op as `params_json`, a verb's
params STAY authored in `#Op` with NO `charly migrate` step and NO cross-repo corpus
sweep when its implementation moves out-of-tree — the plugin reads them from the Op,
exactly as the in-proc `runCharlyVerb` did. `TestInvokeVerbProvider_ExternalCharlyVerb`
proves it: a non-`CheckVerbProvider` verb provider receives `Op{Kube: apply, Namespace:
demo}` intact and its `pluginCheckResult` decodes. The `else`-branch routing is reached
only once a real external verb registers (Phase 1's first verb extraction) — the same
"enabler now, consumer next" shape as E3-kind. R10: `go test ./...` (factoring +
no-migration unit test) + `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora) + check-pod (the
builtin verb-dispatch path unregressed). Observed pre-existing follow-up: the plugin-verb
unit tests depend on global builtin-schema state loaded by a sibling test (pass in the
full suite, fail in a narrow `-run` subset) — its own future cutover (make them
self-contained), non-blocking here.

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): E3-deploy — an external deploy provider drives the deploy flow via the E3b reverse channel

The consumer of E3b: the deploy flow can now resolve a `target:` to an OUT-OF-PROCESS
deploy provider (a grpcProvider, Invoke-only — not a typed DeployTargetProvider) and run
it. `ResolveTarget` (unified_targets.go) keeps the typed path for the built-in targets
(local/vm/pod/k8s/android) and routes an external deploy provider to a new
`externalDeployTarget` adapter (deploy_target_external.go) — a `UnifiedDeployTarget`
whose `Add` calls `grpcProvider.InvokeWithExecutor` with the host's executor served on
the go-plugin broker, so the plugin dials back to run the deployment's ops on the real
venue (the E3b reverse channel).

Proven END-TO-END through the deploy flow: `TestExternalDeployPlugin_ReverseChannelEnd
ToEnd` now also registers the external provider, resolves `target: exampledeploy` through
`ResolveTarget` to the `externalDeployTarget` adapter, and confirms `adapter.Add` drives
the same reverse channel (the plugin's script reaches the host executor) — not just a
direct `InvokeWithExecutor`. R10: `go test ./...` (the real-plugin deploy-flow test) +
`charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora, exit 0 — built-in deploy routing unregressed)
+ check-pod (a pod deploy exercises ResolveTarget). The remaining external deploy
lifecycle — `Del`/`Test`/`Update` over the wire with reverse-op recording, live checks,
and plan-diff update — rides with the Phase-3 promotion of a real built-in deploy target
to an external plugin; the adapter errors clearly on those for now.

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): E3b — the host-served ExecutorService reverse channel (out-of-process deploy/step/builder)

The last Phase-0 enabler: an OUT-OF-PROCESS deploy/step/builder plugin can now drive the
host's live `DeployExecutor` (shell/SSH on the venue) — which holds OS resources that
cannot cross a process boundary — by calling BACK to the host over a go-plugin broker
reverse channel. New proto `ExecutorService{Venue,RunSystem,RunUser}` +
`InvokeRequest.executor_broker_id` (regenerated via `task proto:gen`). Host:
`executorReverseServer` (plugin_executor_reverse.go) serves it by delegating to a
`DeployExecutor`; `grpcProvider.InvokeWithExecutor` (plugin_grpc.go) stands the server
up on `g.conn.Broker` for the synchronous Invoke and passes the broker id. SDK:
`Executor` + `ExecutorFromInvoke` (plugin/sdk/executor.go) dial that id; sdk.go captures
the go-plugin broker on BOTH sides (`servedBroker` plugin-side, `Conn.Broker` host-side
— previously discarded). Built-in providers keep the typed `DeployExecutor` directly
(no wire).

Proven END-TO-END on real code: `candy/plugin-example-deploy` (its own Go module) is
host-built and served out-of-process over `LocalTransport`; `TestExternalDeployPlugin_
ReverseChannelEndToEnd` drives `InvokeWithExecutor`, the plugin dials back through the
broker, runs a marker script, and it reaches the host's executor. Plus
`TestExecutorReverseServer_DelegatesToExecutor` (the host server in isolation). Every
piece is exercised — no dead code. R10: `go test ./...` (incl. the e2e real-plugin test)
+ `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora, exit 0) + check-pod (no transport
regression). The deploy-flow integration that lets a real `deploy:` USE an external
provider (`ResolveTarget` → an `externalDeployTarget` adapter → `InvokeWithExecutor`) is
the E3-deploy consumer, riding with the Phase-3 deploy-target extraction.

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): the command-provider seam — a 6th provider class contributes CLI subcommands

Phase-0 scaffolding: charly's CLI gains a sixth provider class, `command`, so a
non-machinery command can be contributed by its provider (and, in time, an out-of-tree
plugin) instead of being hardcoded on the Kong root. New `ClassCommand` (provider.go +
the `providerClasses` closed set) and `CommandProvider` interface (provider_command.go)
— `KongCommand() any` returns a pointer to a struct whose fields Kong merges into the
grammar via `kong.Plugins`; `builtinCommandBase` supplies the in-proc-only Provider
half. The CLI struct (main.go) embeds `kong.Plugins`, populated from
`collectCommandPlugins()` (enumerates every registered `CommandProvider`, stable order)
immediately before `kong.Parse`. The machinery commands (box/migrate/__plugin/settings/
version/doctor/clean/candy) stay hardcoded on the CLI struct.

The seam is dormant today — zero command providers — so the CLI is byte-for-byte the
same (`charly --help` unchanged); the ~27 non-machinery command migrations ride with
their domains in Phase 1-4 (check/feature with verbs, vm/domain with kinds, the
deploy-lifecycle commands with deploy targets), each becoming a `command` provider +
(when it ships built-in) a `providers:` manifest entry. Coverage:
`TestCommandSeam_PluginCommandInjected` registers a fake command provider and proves
its subcommand is collected and embedded into the REAL CLI grammar (`charly
<probe>` parses and selects it) — the seam works end-to-end even while empty. R10:
`go test ./...` + `charly box validate` + `charly --help`/`version` smoke + check-pod.

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): registry from charly.yml — built-in provider registration driven by the embedded `providers:` manifest

Cutover B of "registry from charly.yml" (the consolidation was Cutover A): built-in
provider registration is now DRIVEN by a `providers:` manifest in the embedded
charly.yml, not a hardcoded Go list. New `providers` document directive (schema/
node.cue `#NodeDoc` + the exclusion regex, regenerated into `spec.DocDirectives` via
`task cue:gen`) — `providers: { <class>: [<word>, …] }` mapping each provider class
(kind/verb/deploy/step/builder) to the reserved words it contributes. The embedded
charly.yml carries the full manifest (all 66 built-ins). `registry_bootstrap.go`'s
`init()` now: parses ONLY the `providers:` directive from `embeddedCharlyDefaults` via
a minimal yaml decode (`parseEmbeddedProviderManifest` — deliberately not the full
node-form loader, which needs the very kind providers this manifest registers, the
bootstrap circularity), gates the manifest ⇄ compiled-in instances into exact
bijection (`manifestInstanceProblems` — a manifest entry with no instance, or an
instance no manifest entry names, both panic loudly), then registers exactly the
providers the manifest names. The Go `builtinProviderInstances` list remains only as
the instance SUPPLIER (Go types can't be constructed from data); the manifest is the
membership AUTHORITY. The node-form loader skips `providers:` as a recognized directive
(the corpus still validates).

Coverage: `TestProviderManifest_EnforcedBijection` proves the shipped manifest agrees
with the instances, that it drove registration (every manifest provider resolves in
the registry), and that the bijection catches BOTH an omitted entry and a stray entry.
R10: `go test ./...` (the init panics at startup on any manifest/instance break) +
`charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora, exit 0 — loader accepts the directive) +
check-pod. External providers continue to declare via `plugin:` candy blocks (already
charly.yml); this cutover covers the built-ins.

### 2026-06-22 — refactor(charly): consolidate the 5 per-class provider-registration init()s into one site

Structural foundation for the charly.yml-declared provider manifest (the next cutover,
"registry from charly.yml"): the five per-class registration `init()`s (verb / kind /
deploy / step / builder_builtins.go) — each a `for _, p := range []…Provider{…}
{ RegisterBuiltinProvider(p) }` loop plus its own bijection gate — are replaced by ONE
list `builtinProviderInstances []Provider` (all 66 compiled-in providers) and ONE
`init()` in registry_bootstrap.go that registers them all, then runs every per-class
bijection gate (verb-provider, method-allowlist, kind-provider, deploy-target, step)
in sequence. Each gate still runs after ALL registration, so it observes the full
registry — the same after-registration guarantee each per-class init() gave for its
own class, now in one place. Behavior-identical (same 66 providers, same gates); the
orphaned `spec` imports in verb/kind_builtins.go are removed. This single registration
site is what the upcoming manifest will data-drive (the loop iterates the manifest
instead of the hardcoded list). R10: `go test ./...` (the gates panic at init if any
provider failed to register) + corpus validate (repo + box/fedora, exit 0) + check-pod.

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): E4 — live-verb providers self-describe their method contract (delete the central switch + liveVerbDispatch)

Phase-0 enabler of the maximal-out-of-tree program: each live-container verb (cdp/wl/
dbus/vnc/mcp/record/spice/libvirt/kube/adb/appium) now OWNS its method contract on its
provider, replacing the central per-verb dispatch. New `LiveVerbProvider` interface
(provider_verb.go) — `Methods() map[string]methodSpec` + `MethodField(*Op) string`;
each provider implements it (verb_method_contract.go) returning its existing
`<verb>Methods` map + its method-selector field. Deleted: the 10-case
`validateCharlyVerb` switch (validate_check.go — now a single
`providerRegistry.ResolveVerb` → `LiveVerbProvider` lookup) and the central
`liveVerbDispatch` map (reserved_registry.go). The method-allowlist bijection gate
(`checkMethodAllowlists`) now reads each allowlist from the registered provider and
runs in the verb-registration `init()` (after registration, mirroring
`checkVerbProviderBijection` — avoids the alphabetical init-order race).

**Closes a validation gap (R1):** `liveVerbDispatch` carried `kube` but the old
`validateCharlyVerb` switch omitted it, so `kubeMethods`' required-modifier specs
(`apply`→Manifest, `wait-ready`→{Kind,Name}, `lb-external-ip`→{Namespace,Name},
`delete`→Manifest, `raw`→Resource) were never validated at config time. The generic
per-provider check covers ALL live verbs uniformly, so kube is now config-validated;
the corpus (repo + box/fedora, exit 0) confirms no config — incl. the k3s-server /
k3s-agent kube checks — relied on the gap.

The `<verb>Methods` maps stay in checkrun_charly_verbs.go (the verb's dispatch data,
used by `runCharlyVerb`) but are now OWNED by their providers via `Methods()`. The
remaining E4 surfaces — serving the serializable method contract over the plugin
`Describe` channel, and physically relocating each verb's map + `.cue` into a dedicated
plugin unit — ride with each verb's extraction in Phase 1 (where an external verb
actually exercises the over-the-wire path; building it now would be untested dead
scaffolding). R10: `go test ./...` + corpus validate (repo + fedora) + check-pod.

### 2026-06-22 — feat(charly): E3 — the kind-class out-of-proc Invoke envelope (external plugin kinds)

First slice of the maximal-out-of-tree "every kind is a plugin" program (plan: `~/.claude/plans/can-ypu-please-
make-hidden-penguin.md`): generalize the verb dual-path (typed in-proc fast / serializable Invoke envelope) to
the KIND class. A built-in kind keeps the typed `KindProvider.DecodeNode` fast path (no JSON — the perf-gate
benchmark measured the envelope at 7.6µs / 76 allocs per op, so the per-entity decode hot path MUST stay
typed); an EXTERNAL plugin kind (which the core has no Go type for) now decodes out-of-process via its
`Invoke(Op: OpLoad)` envelope. Three additive pieces: (1) `classifyDisc` (node_parse.go) recognizes a
plugin-contributed kind dynamically via `providerRegistry.ResolveKind` — only for non-core discriminators, so
the hot path is untouched (it was a "no discriminator" hard error before); (2) `runPluginKind`
(provider_kind_invoke.go) — the kind-class analogue of `runPluginVerb`: assemble the node body → YAML→JSON →
`validateAuthoredPluginInput(ClassKind, …)` against the plugin's served `.cue` → `Invoke` → store the canonical
entity in the new host-internal `UnifiedFile.PluginKinds` slot; (3) `normalizeNodeInto` branches builtin
(`DecodeNode`) / external (`runPluginKind`). `builtinKindBase.Invoke` still errors "in-process only".

Coverage: `TestRunPluginKind_DecodesViaEnvelope` exercises the whole new path LIVE (recognition → validation →
envelope decode → store) and FAILS without the implementation; the gRPC transport itself is proven by reuse
(the verb class, `TestExternalPluginEndToEnd`). R10: `go test ./...` + `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora,
exit 0 — the additive loader change does not regress the core kind path) + check-pod. Follow-ups (own cutovers):
the deploy/step/builder envelopes + E3b's `ExecutorService` reverse-channel; a dedicated external-kind plugin
bed for end-to-end gRPC-kind coverage; then Phase 1–4 extractions.

### 2026-06-22 — refactor(charly): trim two now-unnecessary validate-path checks (post-E1; BF1 folded in)

Two Go validation checks are no longer needed. (1) `validateDownloadTask`'s `extract` enum check + the
`taskExtractValid` map (validate.go) — REDUNDANT now that E1's step gate (`validateNodeFormSteps`) types every
plan step against the closed `#Op`, whose `extract:` enum (_common.cue) rejects a bad value at `charly box
validate` (proven: a download step with `extract: zzbogus` now exits 1 via the CUE step gate ALONE). The
cross-field rules in `validateDownloadTask` STAY in Go — `download:` requires a URL, `to:` required unless
`extract: sh` (proven: removing `to:` still errors `download requires to: destination`). (2) `validate_check.go`'s
`if verb == "port" && c.Port == 0` — STRUCTURALLY DEAD: `VerbsSet` (charly_methods.go) classifies an op as the
`port` verb ONLY when `c.Port != 0`, so `verb=="port"` already implies `Port!=0` — the branch never fired
(this is the former Wave-A **BF1**). Reworded its comment.

**RDD CORRECTION** of the planned "lift the per-task validators into `#RunOp` arms": the `#Op` schema comment
states exactly-one-verb + the cross-field required-modifier rules are DELIBERATELY kept in Go (CUE closes the
field set + types/enums each field; Go owns cross-field). Moving them into a CUE `#RunOp` disjunction would
contradict that documented design AND degrade error messages — a disjunction failure reports a cryptic
"empty disjunction" where the Go validators give precise, actionable messages (`download requires to:
destination unless extract: sh`). So the clean post-E1 deletion is the FIELD-LEVEL extract enum (now in CUE) +
the dead port check; cross-field validation stays in Go where it reads clearly and errors well. Recognizing
that the existing CUE-field-level / Go-cross-field split is already clean is an RDD correction, NOT narrowing
(same class as the P1/P4 corrections).

R10: go test ./... + charly box validate (repo + box/fedora + box/ubuntu, exit 0; bad extract still rejected by
the CUE gate, download→to: still rejected by Go) + check-pod.

### 2026-06-22 — fix(charly): CUE validates plan-step Op fields — close the silent-typo-acceptance gap (E1)

Node-form steps are SIBLING nodes (`<name>: {candy: …, <step>: {run: …}}`); the loader folds them into the
entity's `plan:` only at decode (`assembleEntityBody`), and decode is LENIENT (drops unknown keys). So the
closed `#Step`/`#Op` schema NEVER saw a candy/check plan step — an unknown Op field (a typo like `donwload:`)
or a bad enum on a step PASSED `charly box validate` silently, then dropped at runtime (a latent bug). Proven:
an injected `zz_unknown_op_field` on a candy step exited 0 before this fix.

Fix: `validateNodeFormSteps` (cue_schema.go) re-parses each node-form manifest, folds every entity's (and
nested member's) step children into `plan:` via the existing `assembleEntityBody`, and types EACH step against
the closed `#Step` (which embeds the closed `#Op`). Wired into BOTH validate paths via ONE shared helper (R3):
`validateCandyManifestCUE` (candies) and `validateProjectCUESchemas`' node-form branch (boxes / pods / deploys
/ check beds — previously SKIPPED there, only load-gated by `#NodeDoc`, which accepts step children as `_`). We
validate the STEPS, not the whole entity against its `#Kind`: a `vm:`/`pod:` DEPLOY block carries
deploy-envelope fields (`disposable`/`lifecycle`/`from`/`install_opts`) the workload `#Kind` does not model
(those are `#NodeDoc`'s deploy arm), so whole-entity validation false-positives (RDD-found on
`check-ubuntu-debootstrap-vm`). Steps-only is clean across the whole corpus (189 candies + every box/bed, 0
false positives) AND rejects a typo'd Op field on a candy step AND on a check-bed step (both exit 1 naming the
field). Also corrected the stale `schema/node.cue` comment that named a nonexistent `decodeAndValidateEntityCUE`
and claimed decode types steps against `#Step` (it does not — R1), and updated `node_validate_test.go`'s fixture
off the legacy inline `package:`/`plan:`-as-fields form (which `parseNodeTree` rejects → `charly migrate`) to
the real child-node form. New `TestNodeFormSteps_RejectsStepTypo` is the check-coverage that fails without the
fix. R10: `go test ./...` + `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora + box/ubuntu, exit 0) + check-pod.

The additive step-typo gate (no Go validator deleted yet) — the prerequisite for lifting the load-bearing Go
per-task validators (validateDownloadTask/…) into closed `#RunOp` arms (the next cutover, E1 step 2).

### 2026-06-22 — refactor(charly): delete validateAgentCatalog — redundant with the closed CUE schema (P1a)

The Go `validateAgentCatalog` (unified.go) checked every `kind:agent` entry's `output_format` against
`{"", "stream-json"}` at load. But `agent.cue` already declares `output_format: *"" | "stream-json"` as a
CLOSED disjunction under the closed `#NodeDoc` gate, and `validateNodeDocCUE` rejects an illegal value at
LOAD (non-concrete `Validate()` catches the disjunction conflict → bottom) — BEFORE `validateAgentCatalog`
ever ran. RDD-proven: the new `TestNodeDoc_AgentOutputFormat_RejectedByCUE` shows the CUE gate rejects
`output_format: bogus` and accepts `stream-json`, INDEPENDENT of the Go validator. Deleted: the validator +
its `LoadUnified` call + the now-orphaned `AgentOutputFormatPlain` constant (its only user was the validator)
+ the 3 `agent_config_test.go` tests for it (their intent is now the CUE-gate test). `AgentOutputFormatStreamJSON`
stays (check_loop.go uses it); its const comment now points at the CUE source of truth. R10: the new CUE test
+ `charly box validate` (repo + box/fedora, exit 0 — real agent configs validate without the Go check) +
check-pod (the edited central loader deploys). Wave-1 **P1a** of the charly-core-externalization program — the
ONLY clean externalization in the audit's "P1" bundle; RDD found the other 7 P1 sub-items genuinely CORE
(computed CPU defaults, go-flags CLI tags, runtime constructor defaults, behavior switches, cross-field
validation) — recognizing that is an RDD correction, not narrowing.

### 2026-06-22 — fix(charly): `charly bundle del <pod>` was broken — record-free teardown via `charly remove`

`charly bundle del <pod>` ALWAYS errored `"no container deploy named X in ledger"`. RCA: `PodUnifiedTarget.Del`
(unified_targets_pod.go) was built on a ledger-DeployRecord teardown model that pods never use — the ONLY
DeployRecord writer is `VmDeployTarget` (deploy_target_vm.go:181, `Target="vm:"+name`); a pod bakes its candies
into an overlay image and persists charly.yml state, writing NO deploy record. So `findContainerDeploy` always
returned nil and Del errored before tearing anything down (the bug never surfaced because the check beds tear
down with `charly remove`, not `charly bundle del`). The path was also INCOMPLETE — it stopped+rm'd the
container but never removed the quadlet or the charly.yml entry, and its overlay check
(`strings.HasSuffix(ref, "-overlay")`) couldn't match the real `<name>-overlay:<tag>` ref.

Fixed: Del is now RECORD-FREE. It delegates the container + quadlet + sidecar + charly.yml cleanup to the
canonical `charly remove` path (consistent with the sibling lifecycle delegations Start/Stop/Update — R3), then
drops the deploy's synthesized `<name>-overlay:*` images (the one extra `bundle del` does over `charly remove`;
a shared base ref is never named that, so it is preserved) and cancels any ephemeral TTL lifecycle. DELETED the
dead `findContainerDeploy` (Del was its only caller) and corrected the stale install_ledger.go Target-field
comment (the same false `container:<name>` claim — R5). New regression test
`TestPodUnifiedTarget_Del_DelegatesToRemove` asserts the `remove <name>` delegation.

R10 (live, disposable check-pod): `bundle add check-pod` + config + start → running; `bundle del check-pod` →
EXIT 0, container removed + quadlet removed + charly.yml entry cleaned + base image preserved (was: always
errored). `go test ./...` (incl. the new test) + `task build:charly` green. Surfaced during the
charly-core-externalization triage (the findContainerDeploy follow-up, upgraded from a dead-code note to a real
bug).

### 2026-06-22 — refactor(charly): collapse the duplicated volume host-path strategy into one helper (PP5)

`ResolveVolumeBacking` (deploy.go) carried the bind/encrypted host-path strategy switch TWICE — once for
label-matched volumes (keyed by the short name) and once for deploy-only volumes (keyed by the config name) —
byte-identical apart from that name argument. Extracted to ONE `resolveVolumeHostPath(dv, name, storageDir,
encStoragePath, volumesPath)` helper (R3); both passes call it. Behavior-identical (the only varying input is
now an explicit parameter); no exported-signature change, callers unchanged. The gocryptfs encrypted LIFECYCLE
stays core (a volume-backing provider class was correctly deferred — single backend, deeply wired into
start/quadlet/credential). Also FIXED a standing R1 divergence: two `enc_test.go` comments promised tests at
`deploy_test.go (TestResolveVolumeBacking*)` that never existed — WRITTEN now (table-driven
`TestResolveVolumeBacking_HostPath` covering bind/encrypted × default/host, plus `TestResolveVolumeBacking`
covering named-fallthrough + label-matched + deploy-only), making the comments true. R10: go test (the new
tests) + check-pod (ResolveVolumeBacking drives every pod deploy, fresh `charly update`). Wave-1 **PP5** of the
charly-core-externalization program.

### 2026-06-22 — refactor(charly): delete the dead deploy-target legacy-spelling alias residue (P3)

EDGE-INHERIT / schema-v4 left runtime alias-following for the legacy deploy-target spellings
(`container`→`pod`, `kubernetes`→`k8s`, `host`→`local`), but the runtime NEVER sees them: `BundleNode.Target`
is set only by `bundleTargetForDisc` from the node-form kind at the edge (always canonical
pod|vm|k8s|local|android), `charly migrate` (schema-v4 + target-local) rewrites the legacy spellings
on-disk, and the loader hard-rejects un-migrated configs. The alias-following was pure dead
belt-and-suspenders. Deleted: the legacy-spelling switch arms in `classifyTarget` (deploy_tree.go) and
`classifyNodeTarget` (bundle_add_cmd.go); the now-no-op `canonicalDeployWord` (unified_targets.go); the three
`RegisterBuiltinAlias(ClassDeployTarget, …)` calls (deploy_builtins.go); and — deploy-target being its ONLY
user — the whole registry alias mechanism (the `aliases` map, `RegisterBuiltinAlias`, and `resolve`'s alias
branch in provider_registry.go). Canonical dispatch is unchanged (`resolve` is a plain byKey lookup;
`checkDeployProviderBijection` iterates canonical words). Also corrected a stale migration-status comment that
claimed kinds/steps/builders are "still switch-driven" (C2/C4/C5 landed). KEPT (separate concerns, not this
claim): the name-based fallbacks (a deploy literally NAMED `host`/`local` → local) and the persisted-ledger
`container:`-key reader `findContainerDeploy` (deploy-record state-format, its own future assessment).

R10: go test ./... + check-pod + check-local (each resolves its canonical target through the now alias-free
registry, on a fresh `charly update`). Wave-1 **P3** of the charly-core-externalization program — corrected
from the audit's "route through the registry" (which assumed the aliases were live) to an R5 dead-residue
deletion after RDD proved them unreachable.

### 2026-06-22 — fix(charly): enforce the plugin protocol-version gate on connect (was claimed, never performed)

`buildUnit` (the client-side construction lifting a connected plugin's `Describe` reply into a
`*PluginUnit`) read only `caps.GetProvided()` + `caps.GetSchemaCue()` and SILENTLY DISCARDED the
`Capabilities.protocol_version` + `calver` fields the server sends — while a comment in `connectAndDescribe`
asserted "a gross mismatch is a readable refusal rather than a wire panic." No refusal code existed: a plugin
built against a different charly proto/SDK connected silently and failed later as a wire panic. Fixed:
`buildUnit` now enforces `caps.GetProtocolVersion() == sdk.ProtocolVersion` and refuses a mismatch with a
readable error naming the plugin's protocol, its (advisory) CalVer, and the host's required protocol. CalVer
is NOT an equality gate — plugins are independent repos at independent CalVers, and a same-host builtin served
out-of-process may advertise an empty CalVer (identical binary) — so it is surfaced in the diagnostic only.
The false comment is replaced with a truthful one; `TestBuildUnitRefusesProtocolMismatch` covers the refusal,
`TestPluginGRPCRoundTrip` the accept path. R10: `check-pod` (the external out-of-tree plugin advertises the
matching protocol → bed green with the gate active). Wave-1 **PE4** of the charly-core-externalization
program (`~/.claude/plans/charly-core-externalization.md`).

### 2026-06-21 — fix(charly): `charly vm ssh` connects via the managed ssh_config alias, not `localhost:2222` (cutover-B finding)

`charly vm ssh <name>` reconstructed the ssh invocation by hand — `ssh -p <port> <user>@localhost`, the port
DEFAULTING to 2222 and resolved only from the vm spec's `SSH.Port`. For a `port_auto` VM the auto-allocated host
port lives in `VmDeployState`, NOT the spec, so the resolution missed it and fell back to `localhost:2222` —
connecting to the wrong port. Fixed: `vm ssh` now execs `ssh <vmName>`, the MANAGED ssh_config Host alias
(`charly-<box>[-<instance>]`) published at `charly vm create` (`publishVmSshAlias`), which resolves the user,
the host port (including the auto-allocated one), and the generated key from `~/.config/charly/ssh_config`. This
DELETES the duplicate manual port/key resolution (R3 — the alias is the single managed SSH interface); `-l`/`-p`
still override. Live-verified: on a fresh `port_auto` k3s-vm (resolved port 35423, not 2222), `charly vm ssh
k3s-vm echo …` connected through the alias and ran the command. Found during cutover B's cachyos-vm investigation.

### 2026-06-21 — fix(charly): drop the stale `host` (C) + `box` (D) kind words from the wrong-kind-child gate

EDGE-INHERIT residual cleanup (a cutover-C + cutover-D follow-up). The wrong-kind-child gate's HARDCODED
kind lists had drifted: `node_parse.go` listed `host` among the deployable kinds (cutover C removed the
`host:` venue kind) and `box` among the non-deployable kinds (cutover D merged `box:` into `candy:`), and
`node_bundle.go`'s resource-member error listed `host`. Corrected to the current kinds — deployable:
`pod/vm/k8s/local/android/group`; non-deployable: `candy/distro/…`; resource members:
`pod/vm/k8s/local/android`. `resourceKindSet` itself is CUE-derived (`spec.ResourceKinds`) and was already
correct — only the hardcoded error/comment STRINGS were stale, so there is no behavior change (an invalid
config was already rejected; only the message text was wrong). Live-verified: `charly box validate` on a
wrong-kind-child config now emits the corrected list. The check skill's reserved-kind list drops `host` too.

### 2026-06-21 — feat(charly)!: EDGE-INHERIT cutover D — the `box:` KIND merged into `candy:` (`base:`/`from:` presence = image)

The fourth and LARGEST EDGE-INHERIT cutover, completing the program ("kinds live only at config EDGES").
The `box:` KIND keyword is ELIMINATED — merged INTO `candy:`. There is now ONE entity kind: a `candy:` node
carrying `base:` (an external base) or `from:` (a builder ref) is a full IMAGE (the former `box:`); a `candy:`
with neither is a LAYER fragment. The `charly box build/validate/...` COMMAND family is UNCHANGED (a command,
not a kind — like `charly bundle` survived cutover B).

**The loader.** `candyKind.DecodeNode` routes a `candy:` node by `candyIsImage` (the `base` OR `from` marker
— the corpus has 75 boxes with `base:`, 4 bootstrap builders with `from: builder:…` and no base, and zero
layers using `from:`) into `uf.Box` (BoxConfig) vs `uf.Candy` (InlineCandy) — the existing SEPARATE maps, so
the box⊕candy name reuses (redis, nvidia, jupyter, …) need ZERO renames. `boxKind` is deleted; `box` leaves
`_reservedNode`/`#Node`.

**The schema — the implicit-discriminator hazard the design panel flagged, resolved.** A raw `(#Candy | #Box)`
disjunction is NOT concretely validatable: in CUE a required-but-absent field is INCOMPLETE, not BOTTOM, so a
no-base/no-from layer never eliminates the image arm. Fix: `#Image: #Box & ({base!} | {from!})` (the image arm
REQUIRES base⊻from) and `#CandyValue: (*#Candy | #Image)` — the `*#Candy` DEFAULT resolves it (an image carries
base/from → bottoms closed `#Candy` → `#Image`; a layer → the default `#Candy` wins). `candy.cue`'s `from:` is
removed (it is now an image marker on `#Box`).

**The migration.** New `box-to-candy` step (`renameBoxDisc`: `box:`→`candy:` at every KIND discriminator,
scoped to MAPPING-valued discriminators so a `box:` cross-ref FIELD is never touched) → HEAD `2026.172.0006`;
the corpus is migrated + re-stamped across the superproject + all 5 `box/<distro>` submodules + the per-host
overlay.

**Four production bugs the box/candy merge surfaced, each RCA'd and fixed in this cutover:** (1) `validate.go`
validated images against the now-deleted `cueKindDef("box")` → `box`→`#Box` re-registered as an INTERNAL
validation key (cueKindDefs is not bijective with the kind keywords); (2) the disjunction concrete-validation
(the `*#Candy` default above); (3) `renameBoxDisc` over-reached onto the `box:` IMAGE cross-ref FIELD of
`#K8s`/`#Android` → scoped to mapping-valued discriminators; (4) `applyDiscoveredManifest` had its OWN `candy:`
discovery branch missing the `candyIsImage` check, so discovered IMAGES landed in `uf.Candy` — breaking
`charly box list`/`box build` for every submodule (`&& !candyIsImage(gn)` added). The `AddBox` scaffold is
rewritten from the stale kind-keyed `box:` to node-form `<name>: {candy: {base:}}`. The `candy:`-as-CHILD =
composition behavior (classifyDisc's `asChild`) is correct and preserved — an image/layer can never be a
deploy member.

Docs (CLAUDE.md + 93 SKILL.md + README) swept of the `box:` kind, with strict MUST-form authoring guidance
(an IMAGE MUST be a `candy:` carrying `base:`/`from:`; the `charly box` COMMAND is unchanged). R10 (all
fresh-rebuild gates green): check-local + check-pod + check-k3s-vm + check-arch-vscode-pod +
check-debian-coder-pod + check-ubuntu-coder-pod + check-cachyos-vm.

**Follow-ups found (each its own next cutover):** `#K8s`/`#Android`'s image cross-ref FIELD is still spelled
`box:` (should be `image:`, a cutover-B gap); the `host` kind word still appears in `node_parse.go`'s
wrong-kind-child error message + the check skill's reserved-kind list (a cutover-C residual).

### 2026-06-21 — feat(charly)!: EDGE-INHERIT cutover C — eliminate the `host:` venue kind; rename Calamares `group` → `package-group`

The third EDGE-INHERIT cutover — a ZERO-CORPUS schema refactor (the `host:` venue kind and the Calamares
`group:` both have zero on-disk usage, so there is no migration / re-stamp; the schema change is in-place,
no HEAD bump).

**C.1 — the `host:` venue KIND is GONE.** A remote/host deploy is the `host:` FIELD on a `local:` deploy
(`local: {from: <template>, host: <user@machine>}`), never a standalone `host:` venue node. `#HostValue` +
`#HostArm` are deleted from node.cue; `host` leaves `_reservedNode` + `#ResourceKind`; the `bundleKind`
provider (its last user — `bundle` went in cutover B, `host` now) is deleted; and the DEAD config-derived
`host` disc/target branches (`node_bundle.go` `bundleTargetForDisc`, `deploy_tree.go` `deriveChildExecutor`,
`deploy_chain.go` `appendHopForFlatPath`) are removed. The internal runtime "host" EXECUTION-venue label
(the host MACHINE — a separate concept, not a config kind) is unchanged.

**C.2 — the Calamares package group moves to its own `package-group:` kind.** `group:` is now UNAMBIGUOUSLY
the targetless DEPLOY group (resource members, no own workload — the former targetless `bundle:`); the
cutover-B dual-mode shape-routing in `groupKind.DecodeNode` is gone, and a new `packageGroupKind` decodes
`#Group` into `uf.Group`. `cueKindDefs` realigned: `group`→`#Deploy`, `package-group`→`#Group` (was the
stale `group`→`#Group`, which would have validated a deploy group against the Calamares def — a latent
zero-corpus bug fixed here). The `target.cue` `group?: [...string]` FIELD (package-group names) is unchanged.

Skills + CLAUDE.md swept of the `host:` venue kind + the `group:` dual-mode, and given strict MUST-form
authoring guidance (a host deploy MUST be `local: {host: …}`; a Calamares group MUST be `package-group:`).
The migrate skill table is backfilled with the cutover-A/B step rows + the correct HEAD. R10 (all
fresh-rebuild gates green): check-local + check-pod + check-k3s-vm.

### 2026-06-21 — feat(charly)!: EDGE-INHERIT cutover B — `bundle:` kind eliminated; substrate kinds at the EDGE with `from:`/`image:` cross-refs

The second cutover of the EDGE-INHERIT program ("kinds live only at config EDGES, never in the middle").
The `bundle:` deploy KIND keyword is GONE: a deploy now carries its SUBSTRATE KIND directly at the edge —
`pod:` / `vm:` / `k8s:` / `local:` / `android:` for a workload, or `group:` for a targetless group of
members. The six cross-ref FIELDS `box?`/`pod?`/`vm?`/`k8s?`/`local?`/`android?` collapse to two: `image:`
(the box/OCI image a `pod`/`k8s`/`android` RUNS — the former `box:`) and `from:` (inherit a SAME-kind
template by name — the former `vm:`/`k8s:`/`local:`/`android:` cross-refs). So `bundle:{box:web}`→
`pod:{image:web}`, `bundle:{vm:pg}`→`vm:{from:pg}`, and a targetless `bundle:{disposable:true,…}`→
`group:{…}`.

The substrate kinds serve DOUBLE duty (a `vm:` is EITHER a VmSpec template with `source:` OR a deploy with
`from:`/`image:`), resolved by SHAPE in the loader (`standaloneKind.DecodeNode` routes on `isDeployShape`:
a scalar disc value or a `from:`/`image:` field → a deploy; bare → a template); `group:` is dual-mode too
(the Calamares package group vs a targetless deploy group, routed by resource members). The RDD spike that
opened the cutover proved the CUE DISJUNCTION arm resolves template-XOR-deploy cleanly, so `VmSpec` and
`BundleNode` stay SEPARATE Go types — the ripple is just the cross-ref fields, NOT a 480-ref restructure.
CUE `#Deploy` loses the six cross-refs (gains `from?`/`image?`); `#BundleArm`/`#BundleValue`/the `bundle`
reserved word are deleted from `node.cue`; `group` joins `#ResourceKind` (a deploy group nests members,
its Calamares-subgroup `subgroup:` being a FIELD, not a `group:` child, so no collision). The Go ripple is
the receiver-scoped cross-ref renames (`.Box`→`.Image`, `.Vm`/`.K8s`/`.Local`/`.Android`→`.From`) across
the loader, deploy targets, status collectors, and commands; `inferBundleTarget`/`setBundleCrossRef` are
rewritten (the disc IS the target — no inference) and the `bundle` kind provider deleted. The save-path
serialization (`bundleDiscForEntity`) emits the substrate kind from `Target`.

A new idempotent `charly migrate` step `edge-inherit` (RECURSING into nested members) raises the schema
HEAD to `2026.172.0004`; the whole corpus (the main `charly.yml`, candies, every `box/<distro>` submodule,
and the per-host overlay) is migrated `bundle:`→substrate. The earlier F3 host-overlay-pollution class
DISSOLVES — a check-local bed is now a plain `local:` deploy node, not a `bundle:` carrying a `local:`
cross-ref. Skills + CLAUDE.md swept of the `bundle:` KIND (the `charly bundle` command + the `BundleNode`
Go type are unchanged).

The full bed-roster R10 surfaced a PRE-EXISTING VM-deploy race (NOT caused by the node-form change — the
FIRST deploy passed on the same tree): `check-cachyos-vm`'s fresh-rebuild hit `pacman -Sy: unable to lock
database` because cloud-init's first-boot seed-package install still held `/var/lib/pacman/db.lck` —
`WaitForCloudInit` cleared on a blank/transient `cloud-init status` read before `cloud-final.service`
finished. RCA'd and fixed GENERICALLY for every VM substrate (arch/cachyos/debian/ubuntu/fedora share the
injected `{openssh,curl,tar}` seed packages, so a cachyos-only cloud-init patch would be an R3 sibling
hack): `WaitForCloudInit` now gates on an explicit TERMINAL cloud-init state (done/error/disabled), and a
new R4 `WaitForPackageLock` sync primitive blocks the deploy until no boot-time pacman/apt/dnf process
holds the lock. R10: check-local + check-pod + check-k3s-vm + check-arch-vscode-pod + check-debian-coder-pod
+ check-ubuntu-coder-pod + check-cachyos-vm disposable beds pass on the fresh substrate form (the two VM
beds re-run on the package-lock fix).

### 2026-06-21 — feat(charly)!: EDGE-INHERIT cutover A — step probe verbs `k8s`/`group` renamed to `kube`/`unix_group` (no kind word mid-config)

The first cutover of the EDGE-INHERIT program ("kinds live only at config EDGES, never in the middle").
Two declarative check-step PROBE VERBS reused reserved KIND words: `k8s:` (cluster probe) collided with
the `k8s` deploy substrate, and `group:` (getent unix group / groupadd) with the Calamares `group` kind.
They are renamed to `kube:` / `unix_group:` everywhere — the `#OpVerb` vocabulary + `#Op` fields (`.Kube`,
`.UnixGroup`, the kube verb's `kube_*` modifiers, the `#KubeMethod` enum, all regenerated from the
single-source `schema/_common.cue` via `task cue:gen`), the `VerbCatalog` + `liveVerbDispatch` registry
keys, the verb-provider registrations (`kubeVerb`/`unixGroupVerb`, `runKube`/`runUnixGroup`/`kubeMethods`),
and the CLI subcommand `charly check k8s <method>` → `charly check kube <method>` (`KubeCmd`). The `k8s`
deploy KIND, the `k8s:` bundle cross-ref, and the Calamares `group` kind are UNTOUCHED (only the verb
namespace moved). New machine-checks `spec/TestNoKindWordAsStepVerb` + `TestNoKindWordAsOpModifier` fail the
build if any future step verb/modifier is spelled like a kind word. A new idempotent `charly migrate` step
`probe-verb-rename` (gated on `isStepNode` so only plan-step `k8s:`/`group:`/`k8s_*:` keys move, never the
deploy kind) raises the schema HEAD to `2026.172.0002`; the whole corpus (the main `charly.yml`, candies,
and every `box/<distro>` submodule) is re-stamped and the `check-k3s-vm` plan + `box/arch`'s `group: wheel`
check are migrated. Skills updated with strict MUST-form guidance (a step verb may never collide with a
kind word). Also fixes a pre-existing bed-infra bug surfaced by the R10: `persistBedDeployOverrides` no
longer persists a LOCAL bed to the global per-host overlay — a local bed never runs `charly config` (its
only reason to seed) and its `local:` template lives in the bed's own project, so writing it poisoned every
OTHER project's overlay load (`validateCheckBeds: references local template … not defined`), breaking
concurrent `check-pod`/`check-k3s-vm` runs. Local deploys persist via the install ledger, so the skip is
lossless.

### 2026-06-21 — feat(charly)!: unified plugin schema over the Describe channel — `.cue` single source, zero builtin/external distinction

A plugin's `.cue` schema is now the SINGLE SOURCE used two ways, IDENTICALLY for a built-in (in-proc)
and an out-of-tree (out-of-proc) plugin: at DEV time `cue exp gengotypes` produces the plugin's Go param
struct (the provider decodes `plugin_input` into it, never a hand-parsed map); at RUNTIME the plugin
SERVES its `.cue` source over the Provider `Describe` RPC (the new proto `Capabilities.schema_cue` +
structured `ProvidedCapability{class,word,input_def}`), and the host splices it onto its base schema
(`base ++ plugin`) and validates every authored `plugin_input` against the plugin's def. The host NEVER
reads a candy's `schema/` dir from disk — the schema travels WITH the plugin. Both kinds arrive as a
`PluginUnit{Providers,Schema}` from `PluginTransport.Connect` (`InProcTransport` for a builtin,
`LocalTransport` for an external), so the load/gate/validate code never branches: `registerPluginUnitSchema`
is the ONE load gate (empty / non-spliceable / missing-def → loud failure; builtins gated at process start
via `loadBuiltinPluginUnits`, externals at connect), and `validateAuthoredPluginInput` is the ONE validator,
wired into `runPluginVerb`. The reference built-in moves into charly's module as a self-contained unit
(`charly/plugin/builtins/exampleprobe/`: schema + gen'd params + `Schema()`/`InputDefs`), and the external
example serves via the new `sdk.BuildCapabilities` (embeds + compiles its schema standalone, ships the
source). `task cue:gen` regenerates every plugin's params from its `.cue` (new `schemagen -pkg` flag + a
loop over `charly/plugin/builtins/*/schema` + the in-repo external). The check-runner now loads plugins
from the RESOLVED candy set (`ScanAllCandyWithConfig`, which includes `@github`-fetched candies and carries
each candy's `.Plugin` + `.SourceDir`) instead of `LoadUnified`'s project-local map — so a box that vendors
all its candies via `@github` (every `box/<distro>`) loads its plugins; `buildPluginBinary` flattens an
`@github`-ref candy key to a safe binary filename. DELETED (R5): `compileBasePlusPlugin` (the disk-read
splice), `charly/schema/plugin_example.cue` + `spec.ExampleprobeInput` (the builtin-schema-in-core-spec
path), `buildProviders`, the old `validatePluginInput`, the proto `repeated string provided`. R10:
`check-pod` composes the built-in (`exampleprobe-baked`) AND the external plugin (`externalprobe-out-of-proc`)
— fresh `charly check run check-pod` PASS (steps=10), both plugins dispatching through the unified
schema-over-RPC mechanism, the external out-of-process with its marker round-tripping.

### 2026-06-21 — fix(charly): bundle-node plan steps now run under `charly check live` (the pod path)

A pod bundle's OWN authored plan steps (a bed's `status-shows-pod` check, or any `check:` on the bundle
node) were SILENTLY NOT RUN under `charly check live` — `CheckLiveCmd.Run` (the pod path) merged only the
baked candy/box plan + the per-host deploy overlay, never the PROJECT bundle's plan. The VM path
(`loadVmCheckPlans`) and the local path (`runLocalCheck`) already merged it; only the pod path diverged.
The fix mirrors them: the pod check-live composition now also merges `uf.ProjectBundleConfig()`'s bundle
plan (`projectPlan + localPlan`, the per-host overlay replacing by id) into the set. Found during C0 —
the `exampleprobe` check had to be baked into the box plan to run on a pod bed; with this fix a
bundle-node check runs too. R10: check-pod runs `status-shows-pod` under check-live (previously absent —
check-live went 8→10 steps, PASS); check-local's `status-shows-local` (the already-correct local path)
confirms no regression.

### 2026-06-21 — refactor(charly): InstallPlan steps → provider registry (delete 3 type-switches + dead WalkPlan)

C4 of the plugin program — the LAST switch migration: the 3 per-step type-switches (OCI `emitStep` in
build_target_oci.go, local `execStep` in deploy_target_local.go, the VM `emitPlan` loop in
deploy_target_vm.go) are replaced by the provider registry. Each of the 12 InstallStep kinds is a
`StepProvider` (`step_builtins.go`) with `EmitOCI`/`EmitLocal`/`EmitVM` methods preserving their venue's
EXACT prior behaviour cell-by-cell — the gate checks (RepoChange hard-errors without
`--allow-repo-changes`; services silent-skip without `--with-services`), the per-VM-cell ReverseOp
collection, and the apk/reboot per-venue skips; the per-target `emitX`/`execX` handlers are unchanged.
The dispatch sites resolve via `providerRegistry.ResolveStep(step.Kind())` and call the matching method;
a bijection (`checkStepProviderBijection`) asserts every kind has a provider. The DEAD, never-wired
`walk_plan.go` (`WalkPlan` + `StepExecutor` — a "Phase 1 defined, Phase 2 never done" abstraction
covering only 8 of 12 kinds) is DELETED (R3). Behavior-preserving — proven by the full install/emit/
deploy test suite. R5: `git grep 'case *ApkInstallStep:'` / `WalkPlan` / `StepExecutor` → only
`CHANGELOG/`. R10: check-pod (OCI emit) + check-k3s-vm (VM emitPlan) + check-local (local execStep),
fresh-rebuild.

asserts every check-dispatch `spec.OpVerb` has a provider — the pure-install verbs
(mkdir/copy/write/link/download/setcap/build) are excluded (they render to install steps, not

### 2026-06-21 — feat(charly): plugin-system foundation — ONE unified Provider over the reserved-word registry

First cutover of the plugin program (`~/Atrapub/charly-plugin.md`): a single `Provider`
abstraction keyed by reserved word, generalizing the CUE-single-source reserved-word registry
so every kind/verb (and future deploy/step/builder) is one Provider — in-process (built-in) OR
out-of-process (go-plugin gRPC), resolved identically by call sites (transport-invisible).

- **`provider.go` / `provider_registry.go`** — the `Provider` interface (`Reserved`/`Class`/
  `Invoke` + the `Operation`/`Result` envelope) and `reservedProviders`, keyed by (class, word)
  because a word like `k8s` is both a kind and a verb. `RegisterBuiltinProvider` (init()) +
  `RegisterPluginProviders` (out-of-proc).
- **The generic `plugin:` check verb** — `#OpVerb`/`#Op` gain `plugin`/`plugin_input`; `runOne`
  → `runPluginVerb` → `providerRegistry.ResolveVerb`. An out-of-tree plugin's verb is authorable
  without recompiling `Op`; an unresolved plugin verb FAILS (never fake-greens).
- **Plugins are candies** — `#Candy.plugin:` (`{providers, source}`) + `validatePluginCandy`
  (a builtin provider must be compiled in); a plugin candy needs no install files. The reference
  built-in plugin `candy/plugin-example` provides + tests the `exampleprobe` verb.
- **go-plugin v1.8.0 + grpc v1.61.0 + protobuf** (grpc pinned to go-plugin's k8s-safe minimum —
  forcing v1.81.1 downgraded `k8s.io/client-go` to alpha); `charly/plugin/proto` (the uniform
  Invoke envelope, JSON payloads so `spec` stays the single source) + `taskfiles/Proto.yml`
  (checksum-pinned protoc, reproducible); `LocalTransport` + `charly __plugin serve|list`.

Internal dispatch switches (check-verb / kind / deploy / step / builder) migrate in later
cutovers; the out-of-proc git-repo-plugin lifecycle (ExecutorTransport, runtime schema splice,
label discovery) + the bundle-overlay-step-not-running finding are the immediate follow-ups.
R10: check-pod bakes + runs the `exampleprobe` plugin verb on a disposable bed (fresh-rebuild).
Bumps the `box/fedora` gitlink to the matching bed coverage.

### 2026-06-21 — feat(charly): the init system is a true single-source OCI label (`ai.opencharly.init_def`)

Closes the R3 duplication where the init entrypoint + management commands lived in BOTH the embedded `init:` vocabulary (build-time, but its `entrypoint:`/`fallback_entrypoint:` keys had become DEAD — no runtime consumer after the go-quality cutover deleted `initEntrypointArgs`) AND the hardcoded `wellKnownInitDefs` registry (runtime), because the build-time vocab is unavailable at deploy (only the OCI-label init NAME was).

- **New label `ai.opencharly.init_def`** (`labels.go`) carries a dedicated `CapabilityInitDef` JSON subset — `entrypoint`, `fallback_entrypoint`, `management_tool`, `management_commands` — so build-only `InitDef` fields never leak into the deploy contract. Added per the capabilities recipe: `BoxMetadata.InitDef *CapabilityInitDef` + `CapabilityLabelMap` entry (enforced by `TestCapabilityLabelCompleteness`).
- **Baked at build** in `writeLabels` (`generate.go`) from the vocab-resolved `labelInitDef` (the same `ResolveInitSystem` that already produced `LabelInit`); **read label-first at deploy** — `resolveEntrypointFromMeta` (`start.go`) + `resolveInitDefFromMeta` (`service.go`) consult `meta.InitDef` first.
- **`wellKnownInitDefs` retained ONLY as the legacy fallback** for pre-label images (cannot re-bake an already-built image's labels — R5 doesn't apply to a still-needed backcompat path); its doc rewritten to say so, and the table frozen (new init systems are declared in the vocab, not added here).
- **Capability win:** the dead vocab `entrypoint:`/`fallback_entrypoint:`/`management_*` keys are now LIVE (consumed → label), and **custom init systems declared only in the vocab now work at RUNTIME** (their full contract travels in the label — previously "build-only"). The stale "honored at build only" comments + skill notes are corrected.

Runtime class: `golangci-lint` 0, `go build/vet/test` (5 new tests: round-trip, legacy-fallback for supervisord+systemd, custom-init-at-runtime, capability completeness), `task cue:gen` reproducible, `charly box validate`. R8: a freshly-built supervisord image carries the label (`charly box labels … --format ai.opencharly.init_def` → the resolved entrypoint + management commands) and the deployed quadlet's `Exec=supervisord -n -c /etc/supervisord.conf` derives from it. R10: the `check-pod` disposable bed end-to-end (`PASS`, 10 steps incl. fresh-rebuild; host clean). Bumps the `plugins` gitlink to the matching skill updates.
